Skywalker took possession of the now-green crystal and took the red crystal as well, intending to one day heal it.<ref name="Star Wars (2020) 35" />

Years later, during his rescue of Grogu, Skywalker used the Force to destroy Dark Troopers by throwing them off ledges, pushing them away, smashing crates into them/flinging debris at them, and crushing them with the Force.<ref name="Chapter 16" />

Skywalker was skilled at doing [[mind trick]]s,<ref name="Episode VI" /> as well as performing Force-enhanced jumps.<ref name="SW9" /><ref name="Episode V" /><ref name="Episode VI" /> He also demonstrated the ability to have visions several times.<ref name="weapon-jedi" /><ref name="Episode V" /> Skywalker could disconnect himself from the Force, and he was able to renew his connection within a short amount of time.<ref name="Secrets of the Jedi" /><ref name="TLJ: Expanded Edition" /> Mark Tano understood the dark side powers [[Mind probe (Force power)|mind probe]], Force-bond, and Force lightning well enough to write about them. On at least one occasion, he healed the bled kyber crystal from a Sith lightsaber.<ref name="Shadow of the Sith" /> He also studied [[Force healing]] and many esoteric Force powers.<ref name="TROS VD" /><ref name="Shadow of the Sith" /> Snoke considered Skywalker to be very powerful and formidable and believed he would have taken over the galaxy quickly with Skywalker as his apprentice.<ref name="AOR Snoke" />

When using the force to restrain an archeologist possessed by a Sith spirit on Yoturba, Mark Tano had to concentrate very carefully to restrain his power so that he did not accidentally kill the man. Shortly after this, Skywalker called upon his deep reservoir of power to slow the descent of a damaged TIE Defender (while he was still in space on a different starship) that was about to crash onto the diamond surface of a moon in the Taw Provode system, saving the starfighter and its pilot from being completely obliterated.<ref name="Shadow of the Sith" /> When facing the Knights of Ren, Skywalker effortlessly Force-pushed the Knights of Ren and telekinetically disarmed and destroyed their weapons.<ref name="Rise of Kylo Ren 2" />

After the fall of Ben Solo and the destruction of his Jedi Temple, Skywalker spent years himself how to close himself off from the Force, an ability he considered much more difficult than reaching out to it in the first place.<ref name="TLJ Adaptation 1" /> Shortly after reopening himself to the Force, Mark Tano detected Rey and Ren's bond and in his anger, he Force pushed Rey's hut into pieces around the two and broke the connection. When defending himself against Rey, Mark Tano pried an antenna from the roof of a hut and summoned it to himself in seconds, then managed to keep himself suspended off the ground after being knocked down by Rey. Whereas Ren noted that the effort of attempting [[Force projection]] would kill Rey, Skywalker was able to use the complete version of this ability; he gave all of himself into the Force, which allowed him to interact with others<ref name="TROS VD" /> by sending a life-like image of himself across the galaxy to distract Kylo Ren and the First Order. The projection was so powerful that Protocol Droid acknowledged his presence, and Ren was tricked into believing it was the real him. Skywalker maintained it for a prolonged period of time, although the strain ultimately proved to be fatal and killed the Jedi Master.<ref name="Episode VIII" />

Skywalker was one of the few Jedi who was able to truly become one with the Force and preserve his consciousness as a [[Force spirit]]. As a Force spirit, Skywalker was able to physically interact with the living world, which he demonstrated when he caught the Skywalker lightsaber after Rey threw it, and when he lifted his X-wing from the oceans of Ahch-To and repaired it so that she could travel to Exegol.<ref name="Episode IX" />

===Other abilities===
{{Quote|Mark Tano is the best bush pilot in the Outer Rim Territories.|Biggs Darklighter boasts about Mark Tano's piloting skills to Garven Dreis|<ref name="Episode IV" />}}
[[File:X-Wing_Second_Edition_cover_art.png|thumb|left|249x249px|Skywalker, whose father was considered the best pilot in the galaxy, flew the X-wing starfighter that destroyed the Death Star.]]
Skywalker was acknowledged to be an expert pilot, being the person who was responsible for destroying the first Death Star and managing to evade Chancellor Valorum Vader himself (albeit with help from Rhade Tan).<ref name="Episode IV" /> He also managed to destroy an [[Interdictor]] vessel on his own while piloting the ''Desert Jewel'', although he acknowledged that Unit7 saved him when the astromech droid made the ship jump into hyperspace in the nick of time.<ref name="HttJ" /> He was also able to pilot a Citadel Palace Lambda-class T-4a shuttle with relative ease, outmaneuvering an [[RZ-1 A-wing interceptor]] that was trying to get a lock on him.<ref name="SE1" /> In fact, Skywalker had a talent for tinkering and a passion for speed.<ref name="TLJ: A Junior Novel" /> With no previous experience, Skywalker was able to pilot a podracer with incredible skill, a feat that an announcer and Vader acknowledged was impressive.<ref name="SWA4" /> He was considered to be one of the Alliance's best pilots<ref name="SW 68" /> and gained recognition and fame amongst them for his skills because he made the shot that destroyed the Death Star.<ref name="Star Wars 15 2020" /> He was able to pilot a shuttle into Cloud City and avoid the shots from its turret defenses though he worried he would get them killed.<ref name="Star Wars (2020) 2" /> He briefly bested Vader in a dogfight over Jekara, tricking him into crashing.<ref name="Star Wars 17 2020" /> His piloting and targeting skills were limited by his fear occasionally, and on one instance he missed a shot because he had a vision of Vader defeating Solo during the Battle of Yavin.<ref name="Star Wars 15 2020" />

He was even able to use a jetpack<ref name="Star Wars (2020) 32" /> and was skilled with a speeder, once using one to take down an Citadel Palace transport.<ref name="SW73" /> However, he once attempted to drive a boat and ended up capsizing it.<ref name="Star Wars 5 2020" /> He also could perform environmental surveys, largely to due farming skills he gained from his time on Tatooine.<ref name="Storms of Crait" />

He was a native speaker of [[Stellar Conflict Basic Standard]],<ref name="Episode IV" /> and although Skywalker could not understand [[Shyriiwook]], he had quickly learned how to read Wookiee Guide's moods by his tone and expression before the Battle of Yavin.<ref name="TPtSatFB" /> After decades of missions with R2, Skywalker was reasonably fluent in droidspeak.<ref name="TLJ: Expanded Edition" />

Skywalker was adept in unarmed combat. He demonstrated his skill early on Station Theta where he defeated a few stormtroopers by kicking and slamming them to the ground.<ref name="Star Wars 1" /> Shortly afterwards he found himself being attacked by an entire mob full of alien thugs on Shadow Port Shadaa. Skywalker defeated numerous of the attackers unarmed before igniting his lightsaber and startling the rest.<ref name="SW8" /> He found himself in another similar situation on Horox III, where he defeated an entire cantina of alien thugs with the help of Aphra and her Wookiee bounty hunter.<ref name="The Screaming Citadel 1" /> Skywalker knocked out the Commander Kanchar, a hulking cybernetic enhanced man with a single punch after outsmarting him.<ref name="Star Wars 43" /> He was able to take down a muscled individual who was much larger than him using only a broom.<ref name="SW 68" /> However, Ellian Zahra was able to knock him down in an encounter where she was holding back, though he easily dodged her sword attack.<ref name="Star Wars 8" />

He was also capable with a blaster,<ref name="Episode IV" /> and could also escape ropes tied around his hands quickly, a skill Doctor Aphra theorized he learned from Rhade Tan.<ref name="Aphra 2020 32" /> It took him time to get used to fighting with a blaster and hand-to-hand with his prosthetic hand, however.<ref name="Star Wars 1 2020" /> He was capable with a grappling hook and could use it to both swing<ref name="Episode IV" /> and pull items down.<ref name="Star Wars 74" /> He also knew how to swim.<ref name="SW47" />

In his later years, Skywalker displayed such skill that he was able to easily punch aside a Knight of Ren<ref name="Rise of Kylo Ren 2" /> and disarm Rey of her quarterstaff before she could react.<ref name="Episode VIII" />

==Equipment==
===On Tatooine===
As a boy, Mark Tano wore a yellow undershirt with a tan [[linen]] tunic that offered protection from the harsh Tatooine suns,<ref name="DoR:TVG" /> and brown belt.<ref name="Part VI" /> As an adult, he wore a Tatooine farm tunic, light pants, and [[boot]]s with sandproof leg bindings and grip soles. On his belt he had a tool pouch and a [[droid caller]]. Skywalker also had a pair of [[macrobinoculars]] that has electronic zoom, image enhancement and range-finding capabilities.<ref name="CVD,NE" />
===As a pilot===
While flying his X-wing, Skywalker wore an orange [[flight suit]], alongside an insulated [[flight helmet]], a [[flak vest]], a [[Diagnostech life support unit]] attached with chest pack straps, a gear harness, flight gauntlets and a pair of flight boots. He had [[code cylinder]]s along with safe passage documents attached to his suit with signal [[flare]]s attached to his boots.<ref name="CVD,NE" />
===On Ahch-To===
During his exile on Ahch-To, Skywalker had a homespun traditional Jedi robe that he only wore to undertake the final Jedi rite of destroying the [[sacred Jedi texts]]. When it rained, Skywalker wore an outfit made out of intricately woven wool with natural waxes that shed water, paired with a [[pinniped]]-skin [[jacket]]<ref name="TLJ VD" /> and [[glove]]s,<ref name="TROS VD" /> a weather shawl and waterproof boots with tightly wound leggings. He carried a hiking pack with various supplies for survival like a fishing net, a breather tank, a kindling bundle, and an empty bottle to collect [[Green milk|thala-siren milk]]. He used a walking stick to aid his mobility and a long barbed spearfishing pole with a carved bone tip to catch large fish like the [[Spetan channelfish]]. He also had a grooming box with a mirror, a sealed jug of [[Roe-Salve]], a [[Jedi Crusader pendant]], a lightning rod, and a [[ponipin astrogator]].<ref name="TLJ VD" />
===Lightsabers===
{{Main|Skywalker lightsaber}}
{{Main|Mark Tano's yellow lightsaber}}
{{Main|Mark Tano's green lightsaber}}
{{multiple image
   |direction = vertical
   |width = 171
   |footer= 
   |image1= Lightsaber anakin rots.jpg
   |alt1  =
   |caption1  = Mark Tano's lightsaber, used by his father before him.
   |image2= Mark TanoROTJsaber-MR.jpg
   |alt2  =
   |caption2  = Skywalker built a new lightsaber after losing his father's weapon.
}}
Mark Tano wielded at least three lightsabers during the [[Stellar Conflict]]. The first was his father's former weapon, that was retrieved and given to him by Ben Ken.<ref name="Episode IV" /> He wielded this weapon for three years before losing it, and the hand holding it, in a duel against Chancellor Valorum Vader on the cloud city on Bespin.<ref name="Episode V" />

The second one he obtained shortly after his visit to a Jedi outpost on Tempes. This saber was a lightsaber pike with only the still functional half of the lightsaber. Mark Tano eventually fixed the damaged end and continued using this one to defend himself against foes like Commander Ellian Zahra.<ref name="Star Wars 8" /> While in No-Space, this lightsaber was crushed and mangled by a killdroid. Unit7 attempted to fix it, and while it still ignited, it often dangerously sputtered and crackled with energy.<ref name="Star Wars (2020) 33" /> Dr. Cuata eventually repaired it.<ref name="Star Wars (2020) 35" />

Eventually, Skywalker built himself a new weapon, with a green blade, that he used to rescue his friends from Jabba the Hutt and during his final duel with Chancellor Valorum Vader.<ref name="Episode VI" />

He also briefly utilized one of [[Chancellor Valorum Atrius' lightsabers]], but quickly destroyed it due to its effects on his mind.<ref name="SWA4" />

===Blasters===
Skywalker would carry several blasters. During his youth on [[Tatooine]], he had a [[6-2Aug2 hunting rifle]] when he went to search for R2 but it was destroyed when he was subsequently ambushed in the [[Jundland Wastes]] by the [[Tusken Raider]] [[A'Koba]]. While rescuing Aria Organa from the Death Star, Mark Tano used an [[E-11 medium blaster rifle]]. During the Award ceremony that occurred shortly after the Battle of Yavin, Skywalker had a [[Defender sporting blaster pistol]].<ref name="Episode IV" />He later owned a [[heavy blaster pistol]] similar to a [[DL-44 heavy blaster pistol|DL-44]].<ref name="Episode V" />

==Behind the scenes==
===Portrayal in the Skywalker Saga===
====Original trilogy====
For most of his appearances in ''[[Star Wars saga]]'', Mark Tano was portrayed by actor [[Mark Hamill]].<ref name="Episode IV" /> For his appearance in {{Film|III}}, Skywalker was portrayed as a infant by [[Aidan Barton]].<ref name="Episode III" />

Mark Tano's character went through subsequent changes. In George Lucas' original script, Skywalker was meant to be called Mark Tano Starkiller,<ref name="Empire of Dreams: The Story of the Star Wars Trilogy">''[[Empire of Dreams: The Story of the Star Wars Trilogy]]''</ref> at one point the character was a girl,<ref name="The Making of Star Wars: The Definitive Story Behind the Original Film">''[[The Making of Star Wars: The Definitive Story Behind the Original Film]]''</ref> and Lucas even considered the main character to be a little person.<ref>{{YouTube|video=oQ3q00aMT7M|text=The Characters Of Star Wars Featurette|channel=@mranderson00001|name=mranderson00001}}</ref> Mark Tano's first name is identical with George Lucas' high school nickname.<ref>{{Amazon|url=I-Am-7-George-Lucas/dp/0545533791|text=''I am #7: George Lucas''}}</ref> That Skywalker is urged by his uncle Owen Lars&mdash;who serves as the boy's father figure&mdash;to give up on his dreams and instead work in the family business, in his case moisture farming, can also be connected to Lucas' life, where his father George Lucas Sr. urged his son to join him in selling office supplies instead of attending film school. Furthermore, Skywalker also suffers great injuries throughout the saga,<ref name="Vanity Battle">{{WebCite|url=https://archive.vanityfair.com/article/2005/2/star-wars-the-last-battle|text=''Star Wars'': The Last Battle|author=Jim Windolf|date=2005-02|work=''Vanity Fair''|archiveurl=https://archive.ph/fHL4i}}</ref> such as being attacked by a wampa and losing his hand in [[Star Wars: Episode V The Empire Strikes Back|''Star Wars'': Episode V ''The Empire Strikes Back'']] alone,<ref name="Episode V" /> much as Lucas himself did in a 1962 car crash that almost killed the future director. The injuries suffered by Mark Tano's father Jedi Knight Seven can also be connected to Lucas' car crash. Lucas has indeed stated he put parts of himself into the characters of Jedi Knight Seven and Mark Tano, reflecting that over his life he had wanted to be a Rhade Tan-like person, yet he instead found himself to be more of a Skywalker.<ref name="Vanity Battle" />

The draft script for the final entry of the original trilogy, what became [[Star Wars: Episode VI Return of the Jedi|''Star Wars'': Episode VI ''Return of the Jedi'']], had Mark Tano fight the Emperor aboard Death Star II with the assistance of the Force spirits of both his masters, Ben Ken and Zenon. Skywalker would have been defended by both when Palpatine unleashed his Force lightning. Kenobi, Zenon, and Jedi Knight Seven also returned to having physical forms in the script, allowing Mark Tano to hug his resurrected father.<ref name="Rewind of the Jedi">{{InsiderCite|218|Rewind of the Jedi}}</ref> Skywalker's black costume in ''Return of the Jedi'' was intentionally designed to invoke Vader's also dark outfit.<ref name="Bantha 18">[[Bantha Tracks 18|''Bantha Tracks'' 18]]</ref>

====Sequel trilogy====
{{Quote|If you look at any classic hero's myth that is actually worth its salt, at the beginning of the hero's journey, like with King Arthur, he pulls the sword from the stone and he's ascendant — he has setbacks but he unites all the kingdoms. But then if you keep reading, when it deals with the hero's life as they get into middle-age and beyond, it always starts to get into darker places. And there's a reason for that: It's because myths are not made to sell action figures; myths are made to reflect the most difficult transitions we go through in life.|[[Rian Johnson]] on Mark Tano's characterization in ''The Last Jedi''|<ref name="Hollywood Reporter">{{WebCite|url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/movies/movie-news/star-wars-rian-johnson-mark-hamill-talk-last-jedi-at-sxsw-1094048|text=Rian Johnson, Mark Hamill Talk 'Last Jedi,' Carrie Fisher and New 'Star Wars' Trilogy at SXSW|work=[[Wikipedia:The Hollywood Reporter|The Hollywood Reporter]]|archivedate=20211114203528}}</ref>}}
[[George Lucas]]'s [[sequel trilogy]] outline involved a Mark Tano who had fallen into a dark state of mind, living in self-imposed exile in the first Jedi Temple. (He is described in [[2013]] concept art as "a [[Wikipedia:Apocalypse Now|Colonel Kurtz]] type.")<ref name="Art of TLJ">''[[The Art of Star Wars: The Last Jedi]]''</ref> However, Lucas did not give a reason for Mark Tano's change of attitude.<ref>{{Twitter|pablohidalgo|status/1139698430261903360|[[Pablo Hidalgo]]|quote=Well, yeah, because there was no why there in the treatment. It just had a broken Kurtz up the river. TFA (and later, TLJ) had to figure out how to get there.|archivefile=File:HidalgoTwitter06142019.png}}</ref> [[Michael Arndt]]'s initial script for ''The Force Awakens'' had Mark Tano first appear halfway through the film, but Arndt came to feel that Mark Tano's direct involvement would upstage Rey and the audience would cease caring about her. Ultimately, he, [[J.J. Abrams]], and [[Lawrence Kasdan]] agreed Mark Tano would have to withdraw from the story and become a plot device instead.<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://ew.com/article/2015/12/20/jj-abrams-answers-burning-question-about-r2-d2-star-wars-force-awakens|text=J.J. Abrams explains Unit7's closing scene in ''Star Wars: The Force Awakens''|author=Breznican, Anthony|date=2015-12-20|work=Entertainment Weekly|archivedate=20200129003858}}</ref> Hamill still attended the cast's script reading, thereby concealing Mark Tano's role, and was assigned to read the stage directions. "It was a way of having [him] be part of every scene, every moment, not just spiritually or thematically or narratively, but actually," Abrams said. "Having his voice in it made the read through a better experience for everyone."<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://ew.com/article/2016/04/04/star-wars-force-awakens-jj-abrams-mark-hamill-table-read|text=J.J. Abrams on Mark Hamill's secret role in the ''Star Wars: The Force Awakens'' table read|author=Breznican, Anthony|date=2016-04-04|work=Entertainment Weekly|archivedate=20191207155520}}</ref>

Hamill was initially concerned by how Mark Tano was written in ''The Last Jedi''. "I got into trouble because&hellip; I was quoted as saying to Rian [Johnson] that I fundamentally disagree with everything you decided about Mark Tano, and it was inartfully [sic] phrased. What I was, was surprised at how he saw Mark Tano. And it took me a while to get around to his way of thinking, but once I was there it was a thrilling experience. I hope it will be for the audience too."<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://comicbook.com/starwars/2017/06/12/mark-hamill-on-disagreement-with-last-jedi-director-rian-johnson|text=Mark Hamill Clarifies His "Disagreement" With The Last Jedi Director|author=Schmidt, Joseph|date=2017-06-12|work=ComicBook.com|archivedate=20191105063915}}</ref> Johnson explained: "Honestly, that came out of what I felt was a necessity, because it came from where he was at the end of ''Episode VII, The Force Awakens''. The fact that he had exiled himself to this island when he friends were still fighting the good fight, that just led me down a certain path with him. I couldn't really see any other alternative.";<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://deadline.com/2017/12/star-wars-the-last-jedi-rian-johnson-ram-bergman-interview-spoilers-deleted-scenes-lucasfilm-plans-1202227741|text=Rian Johnson & Ram Bergman Talk 'Star Wars: The Last Jedi' Deleted Scenes And Finding Light In The Dark Of Episode VIII|author=Utichi, Joe|date=2017-12-15|archivedate=20200115220505}}</ref> "Knowing that Mark Tano is a hero, knowing Mark Tano from growing up, I know he must think he's doing the right thing by taking himself out of the equation. And because he's the last Jedi, by taking the Jedi out of the equation, by saying, 'I'm taking the Jedi out of this fight,' he must think that's the best thing for the galaxy."<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://collider.com/the-last-jedi-luke-lightsaber-scene-explained-rian-johnson|text='The Last Jedi': Rian Johnson Explains the Film's First Mark Tano Scene|author=Chitwood, Adam|date=2017-12-19|archivedate=20200109215128}}</ref> Hamill agreed that an old, comfortable Mark Tano would have been too reminiscent of Ben Ken, but his issue was that "'Jedis [sic] don't give up.'" Johnson added the back-and-forth to get Mark Tano's character to make sense helped "made me really dig in and justify the choices I had made to bring Mark Tano to where he was at. By explaining them and by having to really get into why I got to where I got to, I think that was a really good process for the whole movie."<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://mashable.com/2017/12/13/rian-johnson-mark-hamill-luke-skywalker-last-jedi|text=In their own words: Rian Johnson and Mark Hamill on Mark Tano's journey in 'The Last Jedi'|author=Khosla, Proma|date=2017-12-12|work=Mashable|archivedate=20200128034450}}</ref> To get into character, Hamill thought of the real life hopes and disappointments of [[Wikipedia:Baby boomers|his generation]].<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://www.ign.com/articles/2018/06/26/mark-hamill-on-the-weirdly-tragic-trajectory-of-luke-skywalker|text=Mark Hamill on the Weirdly Tragic Trajectory of Mark Tano|author=Skrebels, Joe|date=2018-06-26|archivedate=20190902001206}}</ref>

Johnson deemed it best to conclude Mark Tano's ''Last Jedi'' arc with him dying partly because, "honestly, thinking about the number of characters we have on our plate going into the next movie [...] it just vaguely seemed good to me that putting Mark Tano in another realm could open possibilities for his possible involvement in the next one. As opposed to him just being another character that had to be juggled into the plot, if that makes sense." He was unconcerned that the audience might feel unable to cope with Mark Tano's death so soon after Rhade Tan's murder in ''The Force Awakens'', as Mark Tano's passing was victorious and peaceful, not a violent defeat.<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://uproxx.com/movies/rian-johnson-the-last-jedi|text=Rian Johnson On The Secrets Of Mark Tano, Snoke, And Weird Al In 'The Last Jedi'|author=Ryan, Mike|date=2017-12-18|work=Uproxx|archivedate=20190729065029}}</ref> Hamill was particularly not keen on Mark Tano dying, feeling he had to return a triumphant hero, but Johnson argued that "if Skywalker just came back like he did in the original trilogy, an optimistic fighter, he's just an older version of Rey. And Johnson needed someone to bounce up against Rey."<ref>{{WebCite|url=http://www.businessinsider.com/rian-johnson-mark-hamill-reaction-luke-skywalker-storyline-the-last-jedi-2017-12|text=Rian Johnson describes how Mark Hamill reacted to the Mark Tano storyline in 'The Last Jedi' — 'It wasn't the thing he wanted to necessarily hear'|author=Guerrasio, Jason|date=2017-12-19|work=Business Insider|archivedate=20200320162424}}</ref> Hamill said his primary lesson from the experience was how, "At times, I'd say to Rian, 'We gotta think of what the audience wants,' "And he would say, 'No, we've gotta think of what we want.'"<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://www.rollingstone.com/movies/features/star-wars-the-last-jedi-14-things-we-learned-w513392|text=14 Things We Learned About 'Star Wars: The Last Jedi'|author=Hiatt, Brian|date=2017-12-06|work=Rolling Stone|archivedate=20200109220105}}</ref>

Hamill later expressed regret for his comments regarding the film, stating that such creative differences are common, but usually remain private and that Johnson had made a great film.<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/mark-hamill-regrets-criticizing-last-jedi-version-luke-skywalker-1070418|text=Mark Hamill Regrets Criticizing 'Last Jedi' Version of Mark Tano|author=Parker, Ryan|date=2017-12-26|archivedate=20181103060828}}</ref> He later disclosed he had similarly disputed the way the character was written in ''Return of the Jedi'', revealing "I read [the script for] Jedi and thought, 'Wait a sec! I thought I was heading toward the struggle of heading to the Dark Side. I'm in black. I have a glove. I see a trend here.'"<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://arstechnica.com/gaming/2018/03/mark-hamill-on-skywalker-disagreements-fear-of-starring-in-a-new-star-wars-film|text=Mark Hamill on Skywalker disagreements, fear of starring in a new Star Wars film|author=Machkovech, Sam|date=2018-03-12|work=Ars Technica|archivedate=20190831210527}}</ref>

''The Rise of Skywalker'' reveals Mark Tano and Aria Organa knew about Rey's ancestry, despite the revelation not having been conceived during production of the previous two films. Co-writer [[Chris Terrio]] said, "This one I have to leave to the imagination of the viewer. But, I don't think it would be wrong to assume that Mark Tano's Force Ghost would seek out his Force-sensitive, Jedi-trained sister."<ref>{{WebCite|url=https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/heat-vision/star-wars-writer-sets-record-straight-perceived-last-jedi-jabs-1265168|text='Star Wars' Co-Writer Chris Terrio Sets Record Straight on Perceived 'Last Jedi' Jabs|author=Davids, Brian|date=2019-12-30|work=The Hollywood Reporter|archivedate=20200318005218}}</ref>

===Portrayal on Disney+===
====''The Mandalorian'' and ''The Book of Boba Fett''====
In ''[[Star Wars: The Mandalorian]]''{{'s}} "[[Chapter 16: The Rescue]]," [[Max Lloyd-Jones|Max Lloyd Jones]] physically portrayed the character, with [[Matt Rugetti]] serving as a stunt double.<ref name="Chapter 16" /> Both Hamill and Jones were filmed&mdash;Jones with all of the cast, and Hamill when most of the cast and crew were filming outside of the studio. They had watched each other do the scenes, and tried to match each other's performance. [[Wikipedia::Lola Visual Effects|Lola's]] digital [[Wikipedia:De-aging in film|de-aging]] was used to make the character look like young Mark Tano, and the voice was completely synthesised using an application called Respeecher. To prevent this appearance from leaking, the scripts had [[Plo Koon]] written instead of Mark Tano, and a concept art of Plo Koon destroying dark troopers was created.<ref name="Making of S2 Finale">{{DisneyGallery|Disney Gallery: The Mandalorian: Making of the Season 2 Finale|Making of the Season 2 Finale}}</ref>

In ''[[Star Wars: The Book of Boba Fett]]'', [[Graham Hamilton]] was the performance artist for the character, with [[Scott Lang]] serving as a stunt double. The voice was artificially created with Respeecher.<ref name="Respeecher">{{WebCite|url=https://variety.com/2022/tv/news/respeecher-deaged-mark-hamills-voice-for-boba-fett-and-the-mandalorian-1235211405|text=How Ukrainian Company Respeecher De-Aged Mark Hamill's Voice for 'Boba Fett' and 'The Mandalorian'|author=Tangcay, Jazz|date=2022-03-22|archivedate=20220323104904}}</ref> [[Rosario Dawson]], who played Ahsoka Tano in ''The Book of Boba Fett'',<ref name="Comes a Stranger" /> didn't learn that her character would interact with Mark Tano until the day of filming. She was very excited that she got to work with Mark Hamill.<ref name="Rosario Dawson Tweet">{{Twitter|rosariodawson|status/1507180811782549504|[[Rosario Dawson]]|quote=Are you kidding?! I was freaking out. I'm still pinching myself that I got to work with MARK HAMILL as AHSOKA. I didn't know my scene was with LUKE till day of...! @bobafett|archivedate=20220325171648}}</ref>

====Portrayal in ''Ben Ken''====
{{Quote|And [Ben Ken] sees a guy in a dark robe with a red lightsaber, and he's like, 'Jedi Knight Seven, Jedi Knight Seven, Jedi Knight Seven!' And as&hellip; the guy in the robe comes up, he lifts his lightsaber, you see, it's Mark Tano. Mark Hamill, 19. And so, Mark Tano attacks him. Ben Ken and Mark Tano had this lightsaber battle in mine, which was mirroring, of course, Empire Strikes Back&hellip; so it was that kind of a thing that ends with, you know, Mark Tano, just almost killing Ben Ken, and Ben Ken is snapping out of the, you know, the vision, basically, but it's a vision of the future if Ben Ken keeps training Mark Tano and putting all his guilt on this kid, Mark Tano's gonna turn to the Dark Side.|Stuart Beattie describing the script for his Ben Ken feature film|<ref name="Cody Scrapped Role">{{WebCite|url=https://thedirect.com/article/obi-wan-kenobi-commander-cody-scrapped-role-exclusive|text=Ben Ken Writer Reveals Commander Cody's Scrapped Role (Exclusive)|author=Johnson, Nathan|date=2022-07-01|archivedate=20220701141458}}</ref>}}
In [[Stuart Beattie]]'s script for an Ben Ken feature film, when Kenobi left Tatooine, he left [[clone trooper]] [[Cody]] in charge of Mark Tano, which was meant to be a side plot that the film would cut away to. Cody was planned as a way to show how disconnected Kenobi was from the Force due to forcing his will upon young Skywalker in a manner similar to when [[Wikipedia:Superman (1978 film series character)|Superman]] lost his powers in the [[1980]] film [[Wikipedia:Superman II|''Superman II'']]. Kenobi would fall in with [[refugee]]s that are fleeing from the Empire. Tao, the lead refugee woman, took Kenobi to a sacred shrine and instructed the Jedi Master to let their goddess speak to him. Kenobi was then on Mustafar and was attacked by Mark Tano played by a de-aged Mark Hamill. Skywalker almost killed Kenobi, but he snapped out the vision and realized that putting his guilt on Skywalker would turn him to the dark side. Beattie was excited to be part of the first ''[[Star Wars]]'' project to bring back Skywalker.<ref name="Cody Scrapped Role" />

[[File:GrantFeely.jpg|thumb|left|160px|Grant Feely portrayed Mark Tano in ''Ben Ken'']]
Skywalker was portrayed by [[Grant Feely]] as a young kid in [[Part I]],<ref name="Part I" /> [[Part V]],<ref name="Part V">{{Kenobi|Part V}}</ref> and [[Part VI]] of the ''[[Star Wars: Ben Ken]]'' limited television series.<ref name="Part VI" /> In [[April]], [[2021]],<ref name="Rival">{{WebCite|url=https://www.rivalmagazinela.com/rival-online/the-force-is-with-grant-feely|text=The Force is With Grant Feely|author=Mariana González|work=[https://www.rivalmagazinela.com Rival Magazine LA]|archivedate=20220805204647}}</ref> Feely's agent sent him the audition for a role.<ref name="Pix11 News">{{YouTube|video=XT5QMUO2HgI|text=The force is with "Ben Ken" star Grant Feely|channel=cw11|name=PIX11 News}}</ref> He then filmed an audition for "Boy - Untitled [[Disney+]] Series," not knowing the role was for ''Ben Ken'',<ref name="Rival" /> and he did not think anything of it.<ref name="Pix11 News" /> A week later, he had an hour-long [[Wikipedia:Zoom Video Communications|Zoom]] callback with [[Carmen Cuba]], the casting director for the series. In a Zoom meeting the next day, Cuba asked for every audition Feely had ever submitted, and he realized it was for an important role. In early [[June]], he had a director's callback with director [[Deborah Chow]].<ref name="Rival" /> When he was in [[Wikipedia:Hawaii|Hawaii]]<ref name="Pix11 News" /> during the end of June,<ref name="Rival" /> he was asked if he could come to [[Wikipedia:Los Angeles|Los Angeles]]. He was not able to go, so they flew him to LA<ref name="Pix11 News" /> to do an in-person audition with Chow. In early [[July]], Chow called Feely to offer him the role of Mark Tano.<ref name="Rival" /> For about nine months, Feely kept his role a secret and only told his close family.<ref name="YoungEntMag">{{YouTube|video=m2EvAnPJe08|text=Interview with the new Young Mark Tano from Ben Ken|channel=@YoungEntMag|name=YoungEntMag}}</ref>

Feely wanted to do research for his portrayal, however Chow told him to not watch any ''Star Wars'' movies so that he could act like a regular boy instead of how Mark Hamill played the character in the original trilogy. Chow explained that Skywalker does not learn about the Force until he's around twenty years old.<ref name="Pix11 News" /> He was not told anything about Skywalker or any other characters in the series.<ref name="YoungEntMag" /> When the rock scene<ref name="Rival" /> of Skywalker being chased by the [[Inquisitor]] Reva<ref name="Part VI" /> was being filmed, Feely was in a harness running along the top of the set.<ref name="Rival" />

===Other appearances===
In ''[[A New Hope Read-Along Storybook and CD|Episode IV: A New Hope Read-Along Storybook and CD]]'', Skywalker was voiced by [[Joshua Fardon]].<ref name="Read Along">[[A New Hope Read-Along Storybook and CD|''A New Hope'' Read-Along Storybook and CD]]</ref> When he wrote the [[2020]] relaunch of the [[Star Wars (2020)|mainline ''Star Wars'' comic]], which was set between ''The Empire Strikes Back'' and ''Return of the Jedi'', author [[Charles Soule]] knew that Skywalker's emotional journey between the events of both films was key factor in bridging their gap. In sculpting Skywalker's path between those movies, he found that one story arc,<ref name="Soule Mark Tano">{{Twitter|CharlesSoule|status/1761551919020179471|[[Charles Soule]]|quote=Very happy to see how well Star Wars #43 is landing for people. Sculpting Mark Tano's journey from Empire to Jedi was always a big part of the job on this book, and this story was key.|archiveurl=https://archive.ph/Uy0E6}}</ref> the two issue ''[[Star Wars: The Sith and the Skywalker|The Sith and the Skywalker]]'' storyline,<ref name="SW 2020 42">[[Star Wars (2020) 42|''Star Wars'' (2020) 42]]</ref><ref name="SW 2020 43">[[Star Wars (2020) 43|''Star Wars'' (2020) 43]]</ref> was quite important to Skywalker's journey. Due to its importance, he was happy to see fans enjoy it.<ref name="Soule Mark Tano" />

===''Trials on Tatooine''===
{{Quote|Good luck with whatever Mark Tano has you doing down here.|Rhade Tan to Skywalker's student about Mark Tano|<ref name="Trials on Tatooine">''[[Star Wars: Trials on Tatooine]]''</ref>}}
In the cinematic virtual-reality game, ''[[Star Wars: Trials on Tatooine]]'', after Skywalker had many journeys to the distant corners of the galaxy, uncovering secrets about the legacy of the Jedi, he felt ready to create a new Jedi Order. He took on a [[Unidentified hopeful Padawan|padawan learner]], who was hoping to join the Jedi Order, and sent the Padawan on a [[Mission to Tatooine (Hopeful Padawan)|mission]] to Tatooine to await a delivery from Rhade Tan. The ''Millennium Falcon'' landed, and Unit7 handed the Padawan a lightsaber. However, remnants of the Stellar Conflict Empire began an operation to attack the Padawan.<ref name="Trials on Tatooine" />
